  fields:
  - name: '@timestamp'
    level: core
    required: true
    type: date
    description: 'Date/time when the event originated.

      This is the date/time extracted from the event, typically representing when
      the event was generated by the source.

      If the event source has no original timestamp, this value is typically populated
      by the first time the event was received by the pipeline.

      Required field for all events.'
    example: '2016-05-23T08:05:34.853Z'
  - name: labels
    level: core
    type: object
    object_type: keyword
    description: 'Custom key/value pairs.

      Can be used to add meta information to events. Should not contain nested objects.
      All values are stored as keyword.

      Example: `docker` and `k8s` labels.'
    example:
      application: foo-bar
      env: production
  - name: message
    level: core
    type: text
    description: 'For log events the message field contains the log message, optimized
      for viewing in a log viewer.

      For structured logs without an original message field, other fields can be concatenated
      to form a human-readable summary of the event.

      If multiple messages exist, they can be combined into one message.'
    example: Hello World

    level: core
    type: keyword
    ignore_above: 1024
    description: List of keywords used to tag each event.

:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K    # Filebeat will choose the paths depending on your OS.

:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K    # Set custom paths for the log files. If left empty,
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K    # Filebeat will choose the paths depending on your OS.

:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K#=========================== Filebeat inputs =============================
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K# List of inputs to fetch data.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[Kfilebeat.inputs:
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K# Each - is an input. Most options can be set at the input level, so
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K# you can use different inputs for various configurations.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K# Below are the input specific configurations.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K# Type of the files. Based on this the way the file is read is decided.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K# The different types cannot be mixed in one input
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K#
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K# Possible options are:
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K# * log: Reads every line of the log file (default)
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K# * stdin: Reads the standard in
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K#------------------------------ Log input --------------------------------
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K- type: log
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K  # Change to true to enable this input configuration.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K  enabled: false
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K  # Paths that should be crawled and fetched. Glob based paths.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K  # To fetch all ".log" files from a specific level of subdirectories
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K  # /var/log/*/*.log can be used.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K  # For each file found under this path, a harvester is started.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K  # Make sure not file is defined twice as this can lead to unexpected behaviour.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K  paths:
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K    - /var/log/*.log
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K    #- c:\programdata\elasticsearch\logs\*
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K  # Configure the file encoding for reading files with international characters
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K  # following the W3C recommendation for HTML5 (http://www.w3.org/TR/encoding).
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K  # Some sample encodings:
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K  #   plain, utf-8, utf-16be-bom, utf-16be, utf-16le, big5, gb18030, gbk,
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K  #    hz-gb-2312, euc-kr, euc-jp, iso-2022-jp, shift-jis, ...
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K  #encoding: plain
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K  # Exclude lines. A list of regular expressions to match. It drops the lines that are
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K  # matching any regular expression from the list. The include_lines is called before
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K  # exclude_lines. By default, no lines are dropped.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K  #exclude_lines: ['^DBG']
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K  # Include lines. A list of regular expressions to match. It exports the lines that are
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K  # matching any regular expression from the list. The include_lines is called before
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K  # exclude_lines. By default, all the lines are exported.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K  #include_lines: ['^ERR', '^WARN']
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K  # Exclude files. A list of regular expressions to match. Filebeat drops the files that
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K  # are matching any regular expression from the list. By default, no files are dropped.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K  #exclude_files: ['.gz$']
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K  # Optional additional fields. These fields can be freely picked
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K  # to add additional information to the crawled log files for filtering
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K  #fields:
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K  #  level: debug
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K  #  review: 1
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K  # Set to true to store the additional fields as top level fields instead
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K  # of under the "fields" sub-dictionary. In case of name conflicts with the
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K  # fields added by Filebeat itself, the custom fields overwrite the default
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K  # fields.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K  #fields_under_root: false
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K  # Set to true to publish fields with null values in events.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K  #keep_null: false
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K  # Ignore files which were modified more then the defined timespan in the past.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K  # ignore_older is disabled by default, so no files are ignored by setting it to 0.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K  # Time strings like 2h (2 hours), 5m (5 minutes) can be used.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K  #ignore_older: 0
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K  # How often the input checks for new files in the paths that are specified
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K  # for harvesting. Specify 1s to scan the directory as frequently as possible
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K  # without causing Filebeat to scan too frequently. Default: 10s.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K  #scan_frequency: 10s
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K  # Defines the buffer size every harvester uses when fetching the file
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K  #harvester_buffer_size: 16384
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K  # Maximum number of bytes a single log event can have
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K  # All bytes after max_bytes are discarded and not sent. The default is 10MB.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K  # This is especially useful for multiline log messages which can get large.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K  #max_bytes: 10485760
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K  # Characters which separate the lines. Valid values: auto, line_feed, vertical_tab, form_feed,
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K  # carriage_return, carriage_return_line_feed, next_line, line_separator, paragraph_separator.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K  #line_terminator: auto
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K  ### Recursive glob configuration
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K  # Expand "**" patterns into regular glob patterns.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K  #recursive_glob.enabled: true
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K  ### JSON configuration
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K  # Decode JSON options. Enable this if your logs are structured in JSON.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K  # JSON key on which to apply the line filtering and multiline settings. This key
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K  # must be top level and its value must be string, otherwise it is ignored. If
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K  # no text key is defined, the line filtering and multiline features cannot be used.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K  #json.message_key:
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K  # By default, the decoded JSON is placed under a "json" key in the output document.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K  # If you enable this setting, the keys are copied top level in the output document.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K  #json.keys_under_root: false
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K  # If keys_under_root and this setting are enabled, then the values from the decoded
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K  # JSON object overwrite the fields that Filebeat normally adds (type, source, offset, etc.)
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K  # in case of conflicts.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K  #json.overwrite_keys: false
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K  # If this setting is enabled, Filebeat adds a "error.message" and "error.key: json" key in case of JSON
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K  # unmarshaling errors or when a text key is defined in the configuration but cannot
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K  # be used.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K  #json.add_error_key: false
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K  ### Multiline options
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K  # Multiline can be used for log messages spanning multiple lines. This is common
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K  # for Java Stack Traces or C-Line Continuation
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K  # The regexp Pattern that has to be matched. The example pattern matches all lines starting with [
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K  #multiline.pattern: ^\[
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K  # Defines if the pattern set under pattern should be negated or not. Default is false.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K  #multiline.negate: false
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K  # Match can be set to "after" or "before". It is used to define if lines should be append to a pattern
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K  # that was (not) matched before or after or as long as a pattern is not matched based on negate.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K  # Note: After is the equivalent to previous and before is the equivalent to to next in Logstash
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K  #multiline.match: after
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K  # The maximum number of lines that are combined to one event.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K  # In case there are more the max_lines the additional lines are discarded.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K  # Default is 500
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K  #multiline.max_lines: 500
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K  # After the defined timeout, an multiline event is sent even if no new pattern was found to start a new event
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K  # Default is 5s.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K  #multiline.timeout: 5s
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K  # Setting tail_files to true means filebeat starts reading new files at the end
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K  # instead of the beginning. If this is used in combination with log rotation
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K  # this can mean that the first entries of a new file are skipped.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K  #tail_files: false
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K  # The Ingest Node pipeline ID associated with this input. If this is set, it
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K  # overwrites the pipeline option from the Elasticsearch output.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K  #pipeline:
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K  # If symlinks is enabled, symlinks are opened and harvested. The harvester is opening the
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K  # original for harvesting but will report the symlink name as source.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K  #symlinks: false
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K  # Backoff values define how aggressively filebeat crawls new files for updates
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K  # The default values can be used in most cases. Backoff defines how long it is waited
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K  # to check a file again after EOF is reached. Default is 1s which means the file
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K  # is checked every second if new lines were added. This leads to a near real time crawling.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K  # Every time a new line appears, backoff is reset to the initial value.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K  #backoff: 1s
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K  # Max backoff defines what the maximum backoff time is. After having backed off multiple times
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K  # from checking the files, the waiting time will never exceed max_backoff independent of the
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K  # backoff factor. Having it set to 10s means in the worst case a new line can be added to a log
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K  # file after having backed off multiple times, it takes a maximum of 10s to read the new line
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K  #max_backoff: 10s
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K  # The backoff factor defines how fast the algorithm backs off. The bigger the backoff factor,
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K  # the faster the max_backoff value is reached. If this value is set to 1, no backoff will happen.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K  # The backoff value will be multiplied each time with the backoff_factor until max_backoff is reached
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K  #backoff_factor: 2
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K  # Max number of harvesters that are started in parallel.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K  # Default is 0 which means unlimited
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K  #harvester_limit: 0
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K  ### Harvester closing options
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K  # Close inactive closes the file handler after the predefined period.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K  # The period starts when the last line of the file was, not the file ModTime.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K  # Time strings like 2h (2 hours), 5m (5 minutes) can be used.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K  #close_inactive: 5m
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K  # Close renamed closes a file handler when the file is renamed or rotated.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K  # Note: Potential data loss. Make sure to read and understand the docs for this option.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K  #close_renamed: false
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K  # When enabling this option, a file handler is closed immediately in case a file can't be found
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K  # any more. In case the file shows up again later, harvesting will continue at the last known position
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K  # after scan_frequency.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K  #close_removed: true
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K  # Closes the file handler as soon as the harvesters reaches the end of the file.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K  # By default this option is disabled.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K  # Note: Potential data loss. Make sure to read and understand the docs for this option.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K  #close_eof: false
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K  ### State options
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K  # Files for the modification data is older then clean_inactive the state from the registry is removed
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K  # By default this is disabled.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K  #clean_inactive: 0
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K  # Removes the state for file which cannot be found on disk anymore immediately
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K  #clean_removed: true
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K  # Close timeout closes the harvester after the predefined time.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K  # This is independent if the harvester did finish reading the file or not.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K  # By default this option is disabled.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K  # Note: Potential data loss. Make sure to read and understand the docs for this option.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K  #close_timeout: 0

:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K# Autodiscover allows you to detect changes in the system and spawn new modules

:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K#========================= Filebeat global options ============================
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K# Registry data path. If a relative path is used, it is considered relative to the
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K# data path.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K#filebeat.registry.path: ${path.data}/registry
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K# The permissions mask to apply on registry data, and meta files. The default
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K# value is 0600.  Must be a valid Unix-style file permissions mask expressed in
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K# octal notation.  This option is not supported on Windows.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K#filebeat.registry.file_permissions: 0600
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K# The timeout value that controls when registry entries are written to disk
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K# (flushed). When an unwritten update exceeds this value, it triggers a write
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K# to disk. When flush is set to 0s, the registry is written to disk after each
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K# batch of events has been published successfully. The default value is 0s.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K#filebeat.registry.flush: 0s
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K# Starting with Filebeat 7.0, the registry uses a new directory format to store
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K# Filebeat state. After you upgrade, Filebeat will automatically migrate a 6.x
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K# registry file to use the new directory format. If you changed
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K# filebeat.registry.path while upgrading, set filebeat.registry.migrate_file to
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K# point to the old registry file.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K#filebeat.registry.migrate_file: ${path.data}/registry
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K# By default Ingest pipelines are not updated if a pipeline with the same ID
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K# already exists. If this option is enabled Filebeat overwrites pipelines
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K# everytime a new Elasticsearch connection is established.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K#filebeat.overwrite_pipelines: false
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K# How long filebeat waits on shutdown for the publisher to finish.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K# Default is 0, not waiting.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K#filebeat.shutdown_timeout: 0

:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K  #inputs:

:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K    #reload.period: 10s
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K  #modules:
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K    #enabled: false
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K    #path: modules.d/*.yml
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K    #reload.enabled: true
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K    #reload.period: 10s

:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K#================================ General ======================================
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K# The name of the shipper that publishes the network data. It can be used to group
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K# all the transactions sent by a single shipper in the web interface.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K# If this options is not defined, the hostname is used.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K#name:
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K# The tags of the shipper are included in their own field with each
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K# transaction published. Tags make it easy to group servers by different
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K# logical properties.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K#tags: ["service-X", "web-tier"]
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K# Optional fields that you can specify to add additional information to the
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K# output. Fields can be scalar values, arrays, dictionaries, or any nested
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K# combination of these.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K#fields:
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K#  env: staging
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K# If this option is set to true, the custom fields are stored as top-level
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K# fields in the output document instead of being grouped under a fields
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K# sub-dictionary. Default is false.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K#fields_under_root: false
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K# Internal queue configuration for buffering events to be published.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K#queue:
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K  # Queue type by name (default 'mem')
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K  # The memory queue will present all available events (up to the outputs
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K  # bulk_max_size) to the output, the moment the output is ready to server
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K  # another batch of events.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K  #mem:
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K    # Max number of events the queue can buffer.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K    #events: 4096
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K    # Hints the minimum number of events stored in the queue,
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K    # before providing a batch of events to the outputs.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K    # The default value is set to 2048.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K    # A value of 0 ensures events are immediately available
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K    # to be sent to the outputs.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K    #flush.min_events: 2048
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K    # Maximum duration after which events are available to the outputs,
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K    # if the number of events stored in the queue is < `flush.min_events`.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K    #flush.timeout: 1s
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K  # The spool queue will store events in a local spool file, before
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K  # forwarding the events to the outputs.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K  #
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K  # Beta: spooling to disk is currently a beta feature. Use with care.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K  #
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K  # The spool file is a circular buffer, which blocks once the file/buffer is full.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K  # Events are put into a write buffer and flushed once the write buffer
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K  # is full or the flush_timeout is triggered.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K  # Once ACKed by the output, events are removed immediately from the queue,
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K  # making space for new events to be persisted.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K  #spool:
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K    # The file namespace configures the file path and the file creation settings.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K    # Once the file exists, the `size`, `page_size` and `prealloc` settings
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K    # will have no more effect.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K    #file:
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K      # Location of spool file. The default value is ${path.data}/spool.dat.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K      #path: "${path.data}/spool.dat"
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K      # Configure file permissions if file is created. The default value is 0600.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K      #permissions: 0600
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K      # File size hint. The spool blocks, once this limit is reached. The default value is 100 MiB.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K      #size: 100MiB
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K      # The files page size. A file is split into multiple pages of the same size. The default value is 4KiB.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K      #page_size: 4KiB
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K      # If prealloc is set, the required space for the file is reserved using
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K      # truncate. The default value is true.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K      #prealloc: true
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K    # Spool writer settings
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K    # Events are serialized into a write buffer. The write buffer is flushed if:
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K    # - The buffer limit has been reached.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K    # - The configured limit of buffered events is reached.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K    # - The flush timeout is triggered.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K    #write:
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K      # Sets the write buffer size.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K      #buffer_size: 1MiB
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K      # Maximum duration after which events are flushed if the write buffer
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K      # is not full yet. The default value is 1s.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K      #flush.timeout: 1s
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K      # Number of maximum buffered events. The write buffer is flushed once the
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K      # limit is reached.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K      #flush.events: 16384
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K      # Configure the on-disk event encoding. The encoding can be changed
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K      # between restarts.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K      # Valid encodings are: json, ubjson, and cbor.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K      #codec: cbor
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K    #read:
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K      # Reader flush timeout, waiting for more events to become available, so
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K      # to fill a complete batch as required by the outputs.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K      # If flush_timeout is 0, all available events are forwarded to the
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K      # outputs immediately.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K      # The default value is 0s.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K      #flush.timeout: 0s
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K# Sets the maximum number of CPUs that can be executing simultaneously. The
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K# default is the number of logical CPUs available in the system.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K#max_procs:
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K#================================ Processors ===================================
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K# Processors are used to reduce the number of fields in the exported event or to
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K# enhance the event with external metadata. This section defines a list of
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K# processors that are applied one by one and the first one receives the initial
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K# event:
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K#
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K#   event -> filter1 -> event1 -> filter2 ->event2 ...
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K#
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K# The supported processors are drop_fields, drop_event, include_fields,
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K# decode_json_fields, and add_cloud_metadata.
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K#
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K# For example, you can use the following processors to keep the fields that
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K# contain CPU load percentages, but remove the fields that contain CPU ticks
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K# values:
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K#
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K#processors:
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K#- include_fields:
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K#    fields: ["cpu"]
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K#- drop_fields:
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K#    fields: ["cpu.user", "cpu.system"]
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K#
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K# The following example drops the events that have the HTTP response code 200:
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K#
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K#processors:
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K#- drop_event:
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K#    when:
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K#       equals:
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K#           http.code: 200
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K#
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K# The following example renames the field a to b:
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K#
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K#processors:
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K#- rename:
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K#    fields:
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K#       - from: "a"
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K#         to: "b"
:[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K#
